        }

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;

        }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

In terms of severity, I think this is not a high-severity issue. I don't know why these are SECURITY_DCHECKs and what is their purpose historically. The implication here is that the content isn't laid out and is likely going to proceed to paint and presumably show incorrect data. There is, of course, some non-zero chance that this could lead to other security implications but unfortunately, I don't know of any cases where this happened (or I'm not privy to this knowledge).



<span class="line"><!---->In terms of severity, I think this is not a high-severity issue. I don't know why these are SECURITY_DCHECKs and what is their purpose historically. The implication here is that the content isn't laid out and is likely going to proceed to paint and presumably show incorrect data. There is, of course, some non-zero chance that this could lead to other security implications but unfortunately, I don't know of any cases where this happened (or I'm not privy to this knowledge).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





+pdr, since I recall we've had a similar discussion on a different security issue. Do you recall if we had any action items or resolutions from previous discussions?



<span class="line"><!---->+pdr, since I recall we've had a similar discussion on a different security issue. Do you recall if we had any action items or resolutions from previous discussions?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I personally feel like we should audit what is a SECURITY_DCHECK vs a regular DCHECK and try and revive the knowledge of SECURITY_DCHECK importance and implications



<span class="line"><!---->I personally feel like we should audit what is a SECURITY_DCHECK vs a regular DCHECK and try and revive the knowledge of SECURITY_DCHECK importance and implications<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





All that aside, this bug should definitely be fixed. Joey, do you think you can dig in deeper to see why the marker is being marked dirty here and why the layout isn't triggered on it? I would start the investigation by just logging some layout objects methods to get a sense of what the flow is like through the system and see if there are any unexpected interactions between <details> and its <li>



<span class="line"><!---->All that aside, this bug should definitely be fixed. Joey, do you think you can dig in deeper to see why the marker is being marked dirty here and why the layout isn't triggered on it? I would start the investigation by just logging some layout objects methods to get a sense of what the flow is like through the system and see if there are any unexpected interactions between &lt;details&gt; and its &lt;li&gt;<!----></span>

I did a bit of an investigation and here's what I think happens here:



<span class="line"><!---->I did a bit of an investigation and here's what I think happens here:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Because this has a CQ container, we interleave style and layout. Specifically, we do some style, and then to figure out the rest, we wait until layout.



<span class="line"><!---->Because this has a CQ container, we interleave style and layout. Specifically, we do some style, and then to figure out the rest, we wait until layout.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Eventually, we compute layout of a particular container (details element) and call



<span class="line"><!---->Eventually, we compute layout of a particular container (details element) and call<!----></span>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/ng/ng_block_node.cc;l=496



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/ng/ng_block_node.cc;l=496"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/ng/ng_block_node.cc;l=496<!----></a>



<br>





on the details element



<span class="line"><!---->on the details element<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Note at this point we've laid out the LI and its marker.



<span class="line"><!---->Note at this point we've laid out the LI and its marker.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





The details update call causes us to build the layout tree for the shadow dom in the details element. Among other things, we do LayoutObject::SetStyle on one of the slots (the summary one -- LayoutNGListItem SUMMARY). I'm not entirely sure why this is a LayoutNGListItem, but it is a part of an LI, so maybe that's enough?



<span class="line"><!---->The details update call causes us to build the layout tree for the shadow dom in the details element. Among other things, we do LayoutObject::SetStyle on one of the slots (the summary one -- LayoutNGListItem SUMMARY). I'm not entirely sure why this is a LayoutNGListItem, but it is a part of an LI, so maybe that's enough?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This, in turn, causes us to call 



<span class="line"><!---->This, in turn, causes us to call <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/layout_object.cc;l=3276



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/layout_object.cc;l=3276"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/layout_object.cc;l=3276<!----></a>





 to check if the counter values have changed



<span class="line"><!----> to check if the counter values have changed<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Through some levels of stack, we end up calling this 



<span class="line"><!---->Through some levels of stack, we end up calling this <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/html/list_item_ordinal.cc;l=291



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/html/list_item_ordinal.cc;l=291"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/html/list_item_ordinal.cc;l=291<!----></a>





 to update the list counter values



<span class="line"><!----> to update the list counter values<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Because this is a reversed list, we invalidate all LIs above it in the DOM order. Specifically, we call



<span class="line"><!---->Because this is a reversed list, we invalidate all LIs above it in the DOM order. Specifically, we call<!----></span>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/html/list_item_ordinal.cc;l=216



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/html/list_item_ordinal.cc;l=216"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/html/list_item_ordinal.cc;l=216<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





on the LI item, which ends up calling invalidation on its marker:



<span class="line"><!---->on the LI item, which ends up calling invalidation on its marker:<!----></span>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/ng/list/layout_ng_list_item.cc;l=83



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/ng/list/layout_ng_list_item.cc;l=83"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/ng/list/layout_ng_list_item.cc;l=83<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





This calls blink::LayoutObject::SetNeedsLayoutAndIntrinsicWidthsRecalcAndFullPaintInvalidation which invalidates layout.



<span class="line"><!---->This calls blink::LayoutObject::SetNeedsLayoutAndIntrinsicWidthsRecalcAndFullPaintInvalidation which invalidates layout.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





However, observe that we're already in layout due to CQ interleaving. We're also already past the LI item in the update algorithm since LI happens earlier in the layout order.



<span class="line"><!---->However, observe that we're already in layout due to CQ interleaving. We're also already past the LI item in the update algorithm since LI happens earlier in the layout order.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So the layout algorithm finishes with that LI's marker being marked as dirty, which triggers the assert in this bug.



<span class="line"><!---->So the layout algorithm finishes with that LI's marker being marked as dirty, which triggers the assert in this bug.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





----



<span class="line"><!---->----<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I've tried to eliminate some of the components of the repro case, but I believe it's the minimal case needed for this. I also don't think this is content-visibility related, since the invalidation seems to happen because of CQ. I presume that the test is needed to force the style & layout interleaving, but I'm not confident about that



<span class="line"><!---->I've tried to eliminate some of the components of the repro case, but I believe it's the minimal case needed for this. I also don't think this is content-visibility related, since the invalidation seems to happen because of CQ. I presume that the test is needed to force the style &amp; layout interleaving, but I'm not confident about that<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm going to assign this to andruud@ as the CQ expert since I also don't see an easy solution here: seemingly we would need to rerun layout on invalidated list items which "rewinds" layout algorithm to process an earlier item



<span class="line"><!---->I'm going to assign this to andruud@ as the CQ expert since I also don't see an easy solution here: seemingly we would need to rerun layout on invalidated list items which "rewinds" layout algorithm to process an earlier item<!----></span>

Thanks for the analysis vmpstr. This is bad. (As in incompatible with container queries, not sure if it's really a security issue). It works by accident in the normal case (normal = without UA shadows) because the second layout pass we do to fix up the scrollbar situation lays out the invalidated ::marker. However, if disable scrollbars on the view, we do indeed get the same issue without UA shadows:

However, if disable scrollbars on the view, we do indeed get the same issue without UA shadows:<!----></span>

I think a good solution for this is to let contain:style apply to the implicit list-item counter [1]. That way there is no reason to invalidate stuff above the container boundary. It's possible that it's already intended to work that way (specs don't say explicitly either way). (+Oriol: do you happen to know anything about this?)



<span class="line"><!---->I think a good solution for this is to let contain:style apply to the implicit list-item counter [1]. That way there is no reason to invalidate stuff above the container boundary. It's possible that it's already intended to work that way (specs don't say explicitly either way). (+Oriol: do you happen to know anything about this?)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->Also, note the following related issue: <!----></span>

.

I think the only bad stuff that will happen from this, is that ListMarker's text child won't have the right (i.e. updated) content string. That is not a security issue. Labeling accordingly.



<span class="line"><!---->I think the only bad stuff that will happen from this, is that ListMarker's text child won't have the right (i.e. updated) content string. That is not a security issue. Labeling accordingly.<!----></span>

I think that's already the intention of the spec. display:list-item should change the used value of counter-increment (this can be clarified), and style containment should scope counter-increment.



<span class="line"><!---->I think that's already the intention of the spec. display:list-item should change the used value of counter-increment (this can be clarified), and style containment should scope counter-increment.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Otherwise, there could be circularities, like css/css-contain/container-queries/counters-flex-circular.html but using the implicit list-item counter instead of my-count.



<span class="line"><!---->Otherwise, there could be circularities, like css/css-contain/container-queries/counters-flex-circular.html but using the implicit list-item counter instead of my-count.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<br>





[CQ] Respect contain:style in ListItemOrdinal



<span class="line"><!---->[CQ] Respect contain:style in ListItemOrdinal<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In e.g. a reversed list with automatic ordinals, the style recalc of



<span class="line"><!---->In e.g. a reversed list with automatic ordinals, the style recalc of<!----></span>



<br>





an element may cause invalidation of "previous" LayoutObjects.



<span class="line"><!---->an element may cause invalidation of "previous" LayoutObjects.<!----></span>



<br>





If this happens during interleaved style recalc, then we may dirty



<span class="line"><!---->If this happens during interleaved style recalc, then we may dirty<!----></span>



<br>





LayoutObjects that we're already done laying out.



<span class="line"><!---->LayoutObjects that we're already done laying out.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL addresses this by considering style containment during



<span class="line"><!---->This CL addresses this by considering style containment during<!----></span>



<br>





ordinal calculations in ListItemOrdinal. Instead of always considering



<span class="line"><!---->ordinal calculations in ListItemOrdinal. Instead of always considering<!----></span>



<br>





the enclosing list as the scope for the current counter, we now also



<span class="line"><!---->the enclosing list as the scope for the current counter, we now also<!----></span>



<br>





treat intermediate elements with contain:style as such.



<span class="line"><!---->treat intermediate elements with contain:style as such.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1377644" title="Security DCHECK failed: !NeedsLayout() || ChildLayoutBlockedByDisplayLock() in blink::LayoutObject::AssertLaidOut"><!---->Fixed: 1377644<!----></a>
